Definition of I'tikaf and Requirement of Congregational Mosque
Definition and validity condition for i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of i'tikaf and explain the Hanafi condition that it must be performed in a mosque where congregational prayers for all five daily prayers are held.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is only valid in a mosque that holds the five daily congregational prayers – a masjid jami'.

I'tikaf is a virtuous act of seclusion in the mosque for worship. The Hanafi school, based on explicit hadith evidence, restricts its validity to mosques where all five daily prayers are held in congregation. Understanding this condition is essential for correctly performing i'tikaf and for navigating the differences with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
The passage defines i'tikaf as staying in a mosque with intention (and fasting, for certain types). Note the four components mentioned: staying (al-iqamah), mosque, intention, fasting.
Fasting is mentioned in the hadith as a condition; its exact role is subject to internal Hanafi discussion.
2
State the condition for validity
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, i'tikaf is only valid in a mosque where congregational prayers for all five daily prayers are actually held (masjid jami'). If a mosque lacks this, i'tikaf is not valid.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for fatwa.
3
Examine the evidence
The primary proof is the hadith of Aisha (ra): 'لا اعتكاف الا في مسجد جامع' (no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque). This is a clear textual indication (dalalah qatiyyah) from an ahad hadith (thubut zanni).
The negation structure (لا نافية للجنس) is interpreted as a general negation, establishing the condition.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school permits i'tikaf in any mosque, even without congregation. Understand the practical consequence: a lack of full congregation would invalidate i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school, but would be acceptable according to Shafi'is.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the same hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاعتكاف (۱۱۳۰) هو الاقامة بنيته في مسجد تقام فيه الجماعة بالفعل للصلوات الخمس فلا يصح في مسجد لا تقام فيه الجماعة للصلوة على المختار . ضروری نوٹ : الاعتكاف : علف سے مشتق ہے کسی جگہ شہر نا اور لازم پکڑنا مسجد میں روزے کے ساتھ ٹھہرنے کو یہاں اعتکاف کہا ہے ۔ چار باتوں کے مجموعے کا نام اعتکاف ہے [1] شہر نا[۲] مسجد ہونا [۳] اعتکاف کی نیت ہو [۴] روزہ ہو۔ اعتکاف کرنے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ولا تباشروهن وانتم عاكفون في المساجد تلك حدود الله فلا تقربوها . (آیت ۱۸۷ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں اعتکاف کرنے کی دلیل ہے۔ اعتکاف سنت ہے اس کی دلیل آگے آرہی ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۰) اعتکاف کی نیت سے ایسی مسجد میں قیام کرنا جس میں اس وقت پانچوں نمازوں کی جماعت ہوتی ہوں اعتکاف ہے۔ پس مختار مذہب میں ایسی مسجد میں اعتکاف ) صحیح نہیں جس میں نماز کی جماعت نہ ہوتی ہو۔ تشریح : یہ اعتکاف کی تعریف ہے، کہ جس مسجد میں پانچوں وقتوں کی جماعت ہوتی ہو اس میں اعتکاف کی نیت سے ٹھہرنے کو اعتکاف، کہتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ جس مسجد میں اس وقت جماعت سے نماز نہ ہوتی ہو اس میں اعتکاف کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن عائشة انها قالت السنة على المعتكف ان لا يعود مريضا ولا يشهد جنازة ولا يمس امرأة ولا يباشرها ولا يخرج لحاجة الا لما لا بد منه ولا اعتكاف الا بصوم ولا اعتكاف الا في مسجد جامع (ابو داؤد شریف، المعتلف یعود المریض ص ۱۳۴۲ نمبر ۲۴۷۳ / دار قطنی ، باب الاعتکاف ج ثانی ص ۱۸۱ نمبر ۲۳۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جماعت والی مسجد میں اعتکاف ہوگا۔ (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن حذيفة قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول كل مسجد له مؤذن وامام فالاعتكاف فيه يصلح (دار قطنی ، باب الاعتكاف، ج ثانی ص ۱۷۹، نمبر ۲۳۲۳۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایسی مسجد میں جس میں پنج وقتہ نماز ہوتی ہو اس میں اعتکاف جائز ہے (۳) چونکہ جماعت کے ساتھ مختلف کونماز پڑھنی ہوگی اس لئے جس مسجد میں پنج وقتہ نماز نہ ہوتی ہو وہاں جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنے میں دقت ہوگی ۔
Chapter of I'tikaf. (1130) It is staying with intention in a mosque in which congregation is actually held for the five prayers. So it is not valid in a mosque in which congregation is not held for prayer, according to the chosen view. Essential note: I'tikaf is derived from 'akafa', meaning to stay and confine oneself. Here it refers to staying in a mosque with fasting. The name I'tikaf is given to the combination of four things: (1) staying, (2) being in a mosque, (3) intention of i'tikaf, (4) fasting. The evidence for i'tikaf is this verse: 'And do not have relations with them as long as you are staying for worship in the mosques. These are the limits [set by] Allah, so do not approach them.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187) This verse is evidence for performing i'tikaf. I'tikaf is sunnah; its evidence will come later. Translation: (1130) Staying with the intention of i'tikaf in a mosque in which the five prayers are held with congregation is i'tikaf. So according to the chosen madhhab, i'tikaf is not valid in a mosque in which congregation is not held for prayer. Explanation: This is the definition of i'tikaf: staying with the intention of i'tikaf in a mosque where the five prayers are held with congregation is called i'tikaf. Thus, i'tikaf is not valid in a mosque where prayer with congregation is not held at that time. Evidence: (1) From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that she said: 'The sunnah for the one performing i'tikaf is not to visit the sick, nor attend a funeral, nor touch a woman, nor have relations with her, nor go out for any need except for that which is unavoidable, and there is no i'tikaf except with fasting, and there is no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque.' (Abu Dawud, Dar Qutni) This hadith indicates that i'tikaf is in a mosque with congregation. (2) Another hadith: From Hudhayfah (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Every mosque that has a mu'adhdhin and an imam, i'tikaf in it is valid.' (Dar Qutni) This hadith shows that i'tikaf is permissible in a mosque where the five prayers are held. (3) Because one has to pray different prayers with congregation, so in a mosque where the five prayers are not held, it would be difficult to pray with congregation.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the definition and conditions of i'tikaf. The author begins by stating the chapter on i'tikaf, then gives the ruling: i'tikaf is staying in a mosque with the intention of worship, but the mosque must be one where congregational prayers for all five daily prayers are actually established. If a mosque does not hold these congregations, i'tikaf is not valid according to the relied-upon (mukhtar) position of the Hanafi school. The author then provides an essential note explaining that i'tikaf linguistically means to stay and confine oneself, and technically it is the combination of four elements: staying in a mosque, having the intention of i'tikaf, and fasting (for certain types). The primary evidence from the Quran is verse 2:187, which mentions staying in mosques. The author notes that i'tikaf is sunnah, citing that the proof for its sunnah status will follow. In the explanation, he reiterates the definition and condition, and then provides three proofs: (1) the hadith of Aisha which explicitly states 'no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque', (2) the hadith of Hudhayfah that i'tikaf is valid in any mosque with a mu'adhdhin and imam (implying congregation), and (3) a rational argument that since the mu'takif must attend congregational prayers, it would be difficult in a mosque without congregation. This establishes that the mosque must be a masjid jam'i (congregational mosque) where all five prayers are held with jama'ah.

Key Terms
اعتکاف (i'tikaf): Staying in a mosque with intention and, according to the passage, fasting for the purpose of worship.
مسجد جامع (masjid jami'): A mosque where the Friday prayer and congregational prayers for all five daily prayers are held.
الاقامة (al-iqamah): Staying or residing with the intention of worship in the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) In a mosque that holds the Friday prayer only.
C) In a mosque where all five daily prayers are held with congregation.
D) In any place designated for worship, even at home.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is only valid in a masjid jami' where all five congregational prayers are established, as supported by the hadith of Aisha (ra).

Women's I'tikaf in the Home Mosque
Ruling that women may perform i'tikaf in their home prayer area

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's i'tikaf and explain the evidence from hadith and the rationale behind allowing the home mosque.

Core Idea
A woman's i'tikaf is valid in her home prayer area, following the practice of the Prophet's wives.

This lesson addresses a common question: Can women perform i'tikaf, and if so, where? The Hanafi school, citing strong hadith evidence, permits women to perform i'tikaf in the place they designate for prayer at home. We will examine the ruling, its types, the proofs, and the difference with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: a woman's i'tikaf is valid in her home mosque (the place she designates for prayer).
This is a special concession for women, as they are not required to attend the congregational mosque.
2
Understand the types of i'tikaf
The passage lists three types: wajib (vowed), sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah (last ten days of Ramadan), and mustahabb (other times). Note that fasting is a condition for the vowed type.
I'tikaf in the last ten days is an emphasized communal sunnah.
3
Analyze the evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet's wives performed i'tikaf after him, implying they did so at home. Additional hadith (Anas, 'Itban) show that the Prophet established prayer places in homes.
These narrations are from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim; they are ahad but accepted.
4
Engage with the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school requires i'tikaf to be in a public mosque. Hanafis respond that 'masjid' linguistically includes any place of prostration, and the Prophet's wives' practice confirms this.
The practical consequence: Hanafi women can perform i'tikaf at home; Shafi'i women must go to a mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۳۱) وللمرأة الاعتكاف في مسجد بيتها وهو محل عينته للصلوة فيه (۱۱۳۲) والاعتكاف على ثلاثة اقسام واجب في المنذور وسنة كفاية مؤكدة في العشر الاخير من رمضان ومستحبّ فيما سواه (۱۱۳۳) والصوم شرط لصحة المنذور تشریح : عورت اپنے گھر میں جہاں پنج وقتہ نماز پڑھتی ہے جسکو عورت کے لئے مسجد کا نام دیا جا سکتا ہے اس جگہ میں بیٹھ کر اعتکاف کرے، اور اگر پہلے سے کوئی ایسی جگہ متعین نہیں ہے تو ایک جگہ متعین کرلے اور اس میں اعتکاف کرے۔ وجه : (۱) عورت اعتکاف کرے گی اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة زوج النبي الله ان النبي الله كان يعتكف العشر الاواخر من رمضان حتى توفاه الله ثم اعتكف ازواجه من بعده (بخاری شریف، باب الاعتکاف فی العشر الاواخرص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۲۰۲۶ / مسلم شریف، کتاب الاعتکاف ص ۳۷۱ نمبر ۲۷۸۴/۱۱۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور کے بعد بھی ازواج مطہرات اعتکاف کیا کرتی تھیں ۔ (۲) اور گھر میں مسجد بنائے گی اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے . عن انس بن مالک آن جدته مليكة دعت رسول الله الا الله الطعام صنعته له فأكل منه ثم قال : قوموا فلأصلي لكم ... فصلى لنا رسول الله الا الله ركعتين ثم انصرف ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوۃ علی الحصیر ، ص ۶۸ نمبر۰ ۳۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت کی نماز کی جگہ متعین کرنے کے لئے حضور نے نماز پڑھی (۳) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے. ان عتبان ابن مالک .... وددت يا رسول الله له ! أنك تأتيني فتصلي في بيتي فأتخذه مصلى قال فقال له رسول الله الله سأفعل ان شاء الله ( بخاری شریف، باب المساجد فی البوت ص ۷۴، نمبر ۴۲۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ معذور آدمی جو مسجد نہ جاسکتا ہو اسکے لئے گھر میں مسجد بنانے کے لئے نماز پڑھی۔ (۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ گھر کی مسجد میں اعتکاف کرے . عـــــن عامر قال ان شاء اعتكف فى مسجد بيته (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب من اعتلف في مسجد قومه ومن فعله ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۳۷، نمبر ۹۶۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گھر کی مسجد میں اعتکاف کرے۔
(1131) For a woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house, and it is the place she has designated for prayer. (1132) I'tikaf is of three types: obligatory in the vowed one, sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah in the last ten days of Ramadan, and mustahabb in other than that. (1133) Fasting is a condition for the validity of the vowed one. Explanation: A woman should perform i'tikaf in her house in the place where she prays the five prayers, which can be called a mosque for her. She should sit there with the intention of i'tikaf. If she does not already have a designated place, she should designate one and perform i'tikaf there. Evidence: (1) For a woman performing i'tikaf, this hadith: From Aisha, the wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan until Allah took his soul, then his wives performed i'tikaf after him. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith shows that after the Prophet, his wives used to perform i'tikaf. (2) For making a mosque in the house, this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik that his grandmother Mulaykah invited the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to food she had prepared, and he ate from it, then said: 'Stand, and I will pray with you.' So the Messenger of Allah prayed two rak'ahs with them, then left. (Bukhari) This hadith shows that the Prophet prayed to designate a place for prayer for a woman. (3) Also this hadith: That 'Itban ibn Malik ... said: 'I wish, O Messenger of Allah, that you would come to me and pray in my house so that I may take it as a place of prayer.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'I will do so, if Allah wills.' (Bukhari) This hadith shows that for a person who is excused and cannot go to the mosque, a prayer place is made in the house. (5) In this saying of a tabi'i: From 'Amir who said: 'If he wishes, he may perform i'tikaf in the mosque of his house.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This athar shows that i'tikaf may be performed in the house mosque.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage contains three rulings (1131, 1132, 1133) and their commentary. The first ruling (1131) addresses women: a woman's i'tikaf is valid in the 'mosque of her house', meaning the place in her home that she has designated for prayer. This is a special concession for women because they are not required to attend the congregational mosque. The author then lists types of i'tikaf (1132) and the condition of fasting for vowed i'tikaf (1133). In the explanation, he elaborates on the woman's i'tikaf: she should sit in the place where she normally prays her five daily prayers, which can be called a 'masjid' for her. If she hasn't designated such a place, she should designate one. He provides four evidences: (1) the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet's wives performed i'tikaf after his death, implying they did so at home since they were in their apartments; (2) the hadith of Anas where the Prophet prayed in a woman's home to establish a prayer place; (3) the hadith of 'Itban where the Prophet agreed to pray in his home so he could make it a masjid; and (4) the saying of 'Amir a tabi'i that one may perform i'tikaf in the mosque of his house. These evidences establish that women (and by extension men with valid excuses) can perform i'tikaf in a designated prayer area at home. The passage then moves to the types of i'tikaf and the fasting condition, which are separate rulings but part of the same textual unit.

Key Terms
مسجد البيت (masjid al-bayt): The place in a home designated for prayer, considered a mosque for the purpose of i'tikaf for women.
منذور (manthur): Vowed i'tikaf, which becomes obligatory upon the person who makes a vow.
سنة كفاية مؤكدة (sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah): Emphasized communal sunnah: if some perform it, the obligation is lifted from the community. Here it refers to i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, where should a woman perform i'tikaf?
A) In the congregational mosque of her locality.
B) In the place in her home designated for prayer.
C) Only in the Prophet's mosque in Madinah.
D) I'tikaf is not recommended for women.

Key Takeaway
Women may perform i'tikaf at home in their designated prayer area, based on the practice of the Prophet's wives and the linguistic inclusion of home prayer spaces as masjid.

Three Categories of I'tikaf in Hanafi Fiqh
Classifies i'tikaf into wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of i'tikaf and identify which legal ruling applies to each based on the condition.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is wajib when vowed, sunnah mu'akkadah in last ten days of Ramadan, and mustahabb at other times.

I'tikaf is a spiritual retreat in the mosque. Its legal weight varies depending on when and why it is performed. This passage from Thamaratun Najah provides a clear three-part classification that every Hanafi student should memorize. Understanding these categories helps you fulfill your obligations and maximize reward.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the three categories
Read the Arabic text carefully: واجب في المنذور, سنة كفاية مؤكدة في العشر الاخير من رمضان, مستحب فيما سواه. Commit these to memory.
The order in the text is intentional: first the wajib, then the sunnah, then the mustahabb.
2
Identify the trigger for each ruling
Ask: What makes i'tikaf wajib? A vow. What makes it sunnah mu'akkadah? Performing it in the last ten days of Ramadan. What makes it mustahabb? Any other time.
Sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah means it is an emphasized communal sunnah – if some do it, the obligation on the community is lifted.
3
Connect to practical scenarios
Apply: A person who vows i'tikaf for three days must fulfill it. A person who wants maximum reward should do i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan. A person who does i'tikaf at another time earns reward but not the same emphasis.
This classification is foundational for all later i'tikaf rulings.
4
Distinguish from common misconceptions
Some think all i'tikaf is sunnah mu'akkadah. This passage shows that only the last ten days of Ramadan carry that ruling. Other times are only mustahabb, and a vow makes it wajib.
Memorize the three-part division to avoid confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۳۲) والاعتكاف على ثلاثة اقسام واجب في المنذور وسنة كفاية مؤكدة في العشر الاخير من رمضان ومستحبّ فيما سواه
(1132) I'tikaf is of three types: obligatory in the vowed one, sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah in the last ten days of Ramadan, and mustahabb in other than that.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is a concise ruling statement categorizing i'tikaf. The author enumerates three types: (1) Wajib (obligatory): when a person makes a vow (nadhr) to perform i'tikaf, it becomes wajib upon them to fulfill. This is based on the general principle that vows must be kept. (2) Sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah (emphasized communal sunnah): i'tikaf during the last ten days of Ramadan is an emphasized practice of the Prophet ﷺ. It is sunnah kifayah, meaning if some Muslims in a locality perform it, the rest are absolved, but it is highly recommended that some do it. (3) Mustahabb (recommended): i'tikaf at any other time of the year is merely recommended, not obligatory or emphasized. This classification is foundational for understanding the legal weight of i'tikaf in different contexts.

Key Terms
منذور (manthur): Vowed i'tikaf, which becomes obligatory upon fulfillment of the vow.
سنة كفاية مؤكدة (sunnah kifayah mu'akkadah): A highly recommended act that suffices the community if performed by some.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not emphasized; i'tikaf outside of Ramadan is mustahabb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of i'tikaf is considered wajib (obligatory) according to the passage?
A) I'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan.
B) I'tikaf that is vowed (manthur).
C) I'tikaf on any Friday.
D) I'tikaf in the month of Shawwal.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf has three legal categories: wajib for vowed, sunnah mu'akkadah for last ten days of Ramadan, and mustahabb for other times.

Fasting as a Condition for Vowed I'tikaf
States that fasting is a condition for the validity of vowed i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that fasting is a condition for the validity of vowed i'tikaf and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Fasting is a prerequisite for the validity of a vowed i'tikaf.

This passage addresses a specific condition for i'tikaf when it becomes obligatory by a vow. The author clarifies that fasting is not a general requirement for all i'tikaf but only for manthur i'tikaf. The ruling is supported by a hadith from Aisha (ra) which provides the legal basis. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion between types of i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is vowed (manthur) i'tikaf. The ruling is that fasting is a condition (shart) for its validity; without fasting, the i'tikaf is invalid.
This condition applies specifically to i'tikaf made obligatory by a vow.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith from Aisha (ra): 'La i'tikafa illa bi siyam' (No i'tikaf except with fasting). This is recorded in Sunan al-Dar Qutni.
The hadith is ahad but accepted by Hanafis as evidence for the condition.
3
Analyze the linguistic implication (wajh al-dalalah)
The combination of negation 'لا' and exception 'الا' indicates restriction: i'tikaf is only valid when accompanied by fasting. This is a strong indicator of conditionality.
The Hanafi school takes this literal meaning as establishing a shart.
4
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
The Shafi'i school interprets the same hadith as recommending fasting, not as a condition. They argue the hadith means i'tikaf is perfected by fasting.
This difference leads to practical consequences for validity.
5
Identify the Hanafi position and its application
Hanafis adhere to the literal meaning of the hadith and apply the condition specifically to vowed i'tikaf, not to sunnah or mustahabb i'tikaf.
The Hanafi position is based on zahir al-riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۳۳) والصوم شرط لصحة المنذور تشریح : صرف منت کے روزے کے لئے روزہ شرط ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن عائشة ان النبي عل الله قال لا اعتكاف الا بصيام (دارقطنی ، باب الاعتکاف ج ثانی ص ۷۹ انمبر ۲۳۳۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ روزے کے بغیر اعتکاف نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے، عـن ابـن عـمـر أن عمر قال
(1133) Fasting is a condition for the validity of the vowed one. Explanation: Fasting is a condition only for the vowed i'tikaf. Evidence: (1) From Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' (Dar Qutni) This hadith indicates that there is no i'tikaf without fasting. (2) In this hadith, from Ibn Umar that Umar said...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and evidence that fasting is a condition (shart) for the validity of a vowed (manthur) i'tikaf. The author clarifies that fasting is only required for i'tikaf that is made obligatory by a vow; for other types (sunnah or mustahabb), fasting is not a condition. The primary evidence is the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet ﷺ said 'La i'tikafa illa bi siyam' (No i'tikaf except with fasting). This hadith, though interpreted by some as pointing to perfection rather than condition, is taken by Hanafis as indicating that fasting is a condition for the validity of i'tikaf in the context of a vow. The second hadith from Ibn Umar is incomplete in the text, but it is known in other sources: Umar said to the Prophet, 'I vowed to perform i'tikaf in the Sacred Mosque,' and the Prophet told him to fulfill his vow with fasting. Thus, the condition of fasting applies specifically to vowed i'tikaf.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): Condition for validity; if absent, the act is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) All types of i'tikaf.

Key Takeaway
Fasting is a condition (shart) for the validity of a vowed (manthur) i'tikaf, based on the hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi siyam'.

Minimum Duration of Nafl I'tikaf
Defines the minimum valid nafl i'tikaf and the condition of fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum valid duration of nafl i'tikaf and explain why fasting is not a condition, citing the relevant athar.

Core Idea
Nafl i'tikaf is valid for any short period, even a moment, and fasting is not required unless stipulated.

In this passage, the author addresses a common question: what is the minimum time one must spend in i'tikaf for it to be valid, and must one be fasting? The Hanafi school takes a lenient position on nafl i'tikaf, allowing even a brief stay in the mosque with the intention of seclusion. The key distinction is that for nafl (voluntary) i'tikaf, fasting is not a condition, whereas for a vowed (mandhur) i'tikaf, fasting becomes necessary if stipulated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Category
Recognise that the passage deals specifically with nafl (supererogatory) i'tikaf, not obligatory or vowed i'tikaf. The ruling is about its validity and conditions.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling on Minimum Duration
The text states: 'Wa aqallahu naflan muddatun yasiratun wa law kana mashiyan 'ala al-mufta bih.' That is, the minimum duration for nafl i'tikaf is a short period, even if one is walking. This includes any brief stay.
The mufta bih position is that even a moment suffices.
3
Identify the Condition of Fasting
The passage clarifies that fasting is not a condition for the validity of nafl i'tikaf. It is only required if the person stipulates it upon themselves (e.g., in a vow).
This is based on the athar from Ali and Abdullah (RA).
4
Locate the Dalil
Two athar from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba are cited: (1) Ya'la bin Umayyah performing i'tikaf for 'an hour' (saa'ah) shows a short duration is valid. (2) Ali and Abdullah (RA) explicitly state that fasting is not required for the mu'takif unless stipulated.
Both are ahad athar (zanni thubut) but sufficient for a non-obligatory act.
5
Understand the Thubut and Dalala
The dalil is zanni in transmission but clear in meaning (dalala zanni). It is used to establish the recommended practice (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) rather than an obligation.
The ruling is not wajib; it is about validity.

Explanation: Nafl i'tikaf has two forms: 1) With fasting for a full day. 2) A few minutes' i'tikaf, even while walking; fasting is not a condition; rather, by standing in the mosque and intending i'tikaf, it is performed. This is the mufta bih qawl. Proof: (1) This athar shows that nafl i'tikaf can be for a moment: From Ya'la bin Umayyah that he used to say to his companion, 'Let us go to the mosque and perform i'tikaf there for an hour.' This athar states that if he stipulates fasting then it is necessary, otherwise fasting is not required on the mu'takif.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the minimum duration of nafl i'tikaf. The author states that the minimum valid nafl i'tikaf is a short period, even if one is walking, and this is the relied-upon position (mufta bih). The commentary explains two forms: one with fasting for a full day (like a vow), and another which is a short period without fasting. The key point is that for nafl i'tikaf, fasting is not a condition unless stipulated. Two proofs are given: an athar from Ya'la bin Umayyah shows i'tikaf for an hour is valid; another from Ali and Abdullah explicitly states that i'tikaf does not require fasting to be valid. Thus, the Hanafi position is that nafl i'tikaf is valid with any duration, even a moment, and fasting is not an integral part.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): A supererogatory act of worship, not obligatory.
معتكف (mu'takif): A person who performs i'tikaf, i.e., seclusion in the mosque for worship.
مفتی به (mufta bih): The relied-upon position for issuing fatwas.

Permissible Exits from I'tikaf: The Three Categories
Lists valid excuses for leaving the mosque during i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of permissible exits from i'tikaf and apply the condition of immediacy for exigent needs.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque for a recognized need is permissible and does not break i'tikaf, but exigent needs require immediate transfer to another mosque.

In this passage, we learn that the mu'takif is not confined to the mosque without exception. The Hanafi school delineates three categories of permissible exits, each with its own ruling. We will examine the proof from the Sunnah and understand the critical condition for exigent needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the text and list the three types of needs for which leaving the mosque is allowed: shar'i (religious, e.g., Jumu'ah), tabi'i (natural, e.g., urination), and daruri (exigent, e.g., mosque collapse, danger).
The text uses 'hajah shar'iyyah', 'hajah tabi'iyyah', and 'daruriyyah'.
2
Understand the ruling for each
For shar'i and tabi'i, leaving is simply permissible and one may return after fulfilling the need. For daruri, the ruling includes an additional condition: the mu'takif must immediately proceed to another mosque. If he engages in any other act, the i'tikaf becomes invalid.
The phrase 'fayadkhulu masjidan ghayrahu min sa'atihi' indicates immediacy.
3
Analyze the dalil
The text provides a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) left the mosque to accompany Safiyyah to her house while in i'tikaf. This demonstrates that leaving for a legitimate need (here, fulfilling a request) does not break i'tikaf.
The hadith is from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq (no. 8096). It shows permissibility, not obligation.
4
Note the practical difference (thamarah)
The Hanafi school includes shar'i needs like Jumu'ah as permissible exits, while some other schools restrict exits to only absolute necessities. This difference affects daily practice.
The cross-madhhab dispute is noted in the hanafi_position_box.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۱۳۵) ولا يخرج منه الا للحاجة الشرعية كالجمعة او طبعية كالبول (۱۱۳۶) او ضروريّة كانهدام المسجد واخراج ظالم کرها وتفرّق اهله وخوف على نفسه او متاعه من المكابرين فيدخل مسجدا غيره من ساعته. تشریح : یہاں اضطراری ضرورت کی پانچ مثالیں دے رہے ہیں۔ کوئی مجبوری آجائے تب بھی معتکف کے لئے مسجد سے نکلنا جائز ہے [1] مثلا مسجد گر جائے تو معتکف کے لئے اس مسجد سے نکلنا جائز ہے، لیکن نکل کر فورا دوسری مسجد کی طرف روانہ ہو جائے ، پس اگر کسی دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہوا تو اعتکاف فاسد ہو جائے گا ۔ [۲] یا کوئی ظالم معتکف کو جبرا مسجد سے نکال دے۔[۳] یا مسجد کے پاس رہنے والے ایسے بکھر گئے کہ جماعت کی نماز نہیں ہوتی ۔ (۴) یا ظالموں کی جانب سے جان کا خطرہ ہے، یا مال چوری ہونے کا خطرہ ہے تو ایسی مجبوری میں مسجد سے نکلنا جائز ہے، لیکن اسی وقت دوسری مسجد میں چلا جائے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مجبوری سے آپ مسجد سے باہر نکلے۔ عن ابن المعلى ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان معتكفا في المسجد فاجتمع نساؤه اليه ثم تفرقن فقال لصفية ابنة حيى اقلبک لی بیتک فذهب معها حتى ادخلها بيتها و هو معتكف (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب خروج النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم فی اعتکافه، ج رابع ص ۲۷۷، نمبر ۸۰۹۶) لغت : ضروریة : جو ضرورت کسی مجبوری سے پیش آجائے۔ انھدام گر جانا۔ تفرق: فرق سے مشتق ہے، بکھر جانا۔ مکابر : کبر سے مشتق ہے، تکبر کرنے والے، ظالم لوگ۔
Translation (1135): And he should not leave it except for a shar'i need like Jumu'ah, or a natural need like urine. (1136) Or an exigent need such as the mosque collapsing, or an oppressor expelling him by force, or his people dispersing, or fear for himself or his property from the arrogant ones; then he should enter another mosque immediately. Explanation: Here five examples of exigent need are given. If a constraint occurs, then it is permissible for the mu'takif to leave the mosque: 1) e.g., if the mosque collapses, he may leave but should immediately proceed to another mosque; if he engages in another act, his i'tikaf becomes invalid. 2) Or if an oppressor forces him out. 3) Or if the people around the mosque scatter so that congregational prayer is not held. 4) Or if there is fear for life from oppressors, or fear of theft of property; then in such constraint leaving is permissible, but he should go immediately to another mosque. Proof: This hadith shows that out of necessity the Prophet left the mosque. From Ibn al-Mu'alla that the Prophet was in i'tikaf in the mosque, then his wives gathered to him, then dispersed, and he said to Safiyyah bint Huyayy: 'Accompany me to your house,' so he went with her until he entered her house while in i'tikaf. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Khuruj al-Nabi fi I'tikafihi, vol. 4, p. 277, no. 8096) Vocabulary: ضروریة: need that arises from constraint. انھدام: collapsing. تفرق: from فرق, dispersing. مکابر: from كبر, arrogant people, oppressors.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the permissible exits from i'tikaf. The text divides exits into three categories: shar'i needs (like Jumu'ah), natural needs (such as urination), and exigent needs (like mosque collapse, expulsion, danger). For exigent needs, the mu'takif must immediately enter another mosque; if he gets involved in other matters, i'tikaf breaks. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet left the mosque to accompany Safiyyah home, demonstrating that leaving for a legitimate need does not invalidate i'tikaf. The commentary emphasizes that such exits are allowed only for genuine necessity and should be minimal.

Key Terms
حاجة شرعية (hajah shar'iyyah): A religiously recognized need, such as performing Jumu'ah prayer.
حاجة طبعية (hajah tabi'iyyah): A natural biological need, such as urination or defecation.
ضرورية (daruriyyah): An exigent or emergency need that threatens life, property, or the ability to continue i'tikaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Perform two raka'at
D) Make up the missed time

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits three categories of exits from i'tikaf; the key condition for exigent needs is immediate transfer to another mosque without engaging in other acts.

Exit Without Excuse Invalidates I'tikaf
Ruling on exit without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on exiting i'tikaf without excuse and DISTINGUISH between the consequences for wajib (vowed) and nafl (voluntary) i'tikaf.

Core Idea
Any unauthorized exit, even briefly, invalidates wajib i'tikaf and ends nafl i'tikaf.

This passage addresses a critical aspect of i'tikaf: the effect of leaving the mosque without a valid excuse. The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligatory (vowed) i'tikaf, which becomes invalid and requires restart, and supererogatory i'tikaf, which simply ends. The text also hints at an intra-madhhab difference involving Imam Abu Hanifa's students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, though their view is not fully preserved here.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of i'tikaf
First, determine whether the i'tikaf is wajib (by vow) or nafl (voluntary). The ruling depends on this classification.
The text explicitly contrasts 'fasada al-wajib' (the wajib becomes corrupt) with 'intahaa bihi ghayruh' (the other [nafl] ends).
2
State the consequence for each type
For wajib i'tikaf, the exit without excuse makes it 'fasada' — it becomes corrupt (batil) and must be repeated (qada). For nafl, it simply ends; no make-up required.
Fasada means the i'tikaf is void; the vow is broken and must be fulfilled later.
3
Identify the trigger condition
The ruling is triggered by exiting the mosque 'without an excuse' (bila 'udhr). Any non-necessity exit, even for a moment, invalidates.
Valid excuses typically include urgent bodily needs, fear for life, or being forced out.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) reportedly had a differing view, possibly considering a brief unintentional exit as not invalidating. The text cuts off, so their exact position is not fully captured here.
Later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidayah) clarify that the Sahibayn differentiated between deliberate and accidental short exits.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that any unauthorized exit, even if brief, invalidates wajib i'tikaf. For nafl, it ends the i'tikaf.
The view of Imam Abu Hanifa is taken as the stronger, more precautionary position.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۱۱۳۷) فإن خرج ساعة بلا عذر فسد الواجب وانتهى به غيره. تشریح : بغیر انسانی ضرورت یا مجبوری کے ایک گھڑی بھی مسجد سے نکلے گا تو اعتکاف ختم ہو جائے گا۔ البتہ صاحبین کی رائے...
Translation (1137): If he leaves for an hour without an excuse, then wajib i'tikaf becomes corrupt (invalid), and with other than it, it ends. Explanation: If he leaves the mosque for a moment without human necessity or constraint, then i'tikaf will end. However, the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the invalidation of i'tikaf due to unauthorized exit. The text states that leaving for even an hour without a valid excuse corrupts wajib i'tikaf (i.e., a vowed i'tikaf), and for nafl i'tikaf, it simply ends. The commentary confirms that any exit without necessity invalidates. The passage then mentions that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) have a differing view, but the text cuts off, so their exact position is not fully given in this excerpt. In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that any unnecessary exit, even brief, breaks i'tikaf.

Key Terms
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two prominent students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
فسد الواجب (fasada al-wajib): The wajib i'tikaf becomes corrupt and must be repeated if vowed; it is not simply ended but null and void.
انتهى به غيره (intahaa bihi ghayruh): For non-wajib (nafl), the i'tikaf simply ends; no qada is required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The i'tikaf continues as long as he returns within the same day.
C) He must fast for three days.
D) He may continue from where he left off.

Key Takeaway
Any unauthorized exit from the mosque, even for a moment, invalidates wajib i'tikaf and ends nafl i'tikaf, with the mufta bihi following Abu Hanifa's strict view.

Ruling on Buying and Selling in I'tikaf
Ruling on trade in mosque during i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bringing trade goods into the mosque during i'tikaf and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Trade transactions in the mosque during i'tikaf are makruh tanzih, not haram.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter of I'tikaf: the disapproval of buying and selling while in seclusion for worship. Understanding this ruling helps preserve the sanctity of i'tikaf and clarifies the boundaries of permissible actions in the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is bringing trade goods or concluding sales during i'tikaf. The ruling is makruh (disapproved).
The text uses 'karih' (كراهة).
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one commands keeping mosques free from buying and selling; the other prohibits it outright.
Hadith from Wathila and from Amr ibn Shu'ayb.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'جنبوا بيعكم' (keep away your buying and selling) and 'نهى عن الشراء والبيع' (prohibited buying and selling) show that these actions are disapproved in mosques.
The prohibition applies to the mu'takif who is staying in the mosque.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may consider it haram, but the Hanafi school classifies it as makruh tanzih due to the zanni nature of the evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is makruh tanzih, as recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

باب الاعتكاف (١١٣٩) وكره احضار المبيع فيه وكره عقد ما كان للتجارة تشریح : مختلف کے لئے مسجد میں بیج کے سامان کالا نا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اس سے اعتکاف کے بجائے تجارت کا ماحول بن جائے گا۔ اور ضرورت نہ ہوتو خرید وفروخت کی بات کرنا بھی مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن واثلة بن الأسقع أن النبي عله قال : جنبوا مساجدكم صبيانكم، و مجانينكم ، و شراركم ، و بيعكم ، و خصوماتكم ، و رفع اصواتكم و اقامة حدود كم، و سل سيوفكم ، و اتخذوا على ابوابها المطاهر، و جمروها في الجمع - (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما یکرہ فی المساجد ، ص ١٠٧ نمبر ٧٥٠) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اپنے بیع وشراء سے مسجدوں کو پاک رکھو اس لئے اس کو مشغلہ بنانا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے . عن عمرو ابن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده أن رسول الله الله نهى عن الشراء و البيع في المسجد ۔(ابوداود شریف، باب التخلق يوم الجمعة قبل الصلوۃ ص ١٦٣ نمبر ۰۷۹ ارترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء في كراهية البيع والشراء وانشاد الضالة والشعر في المسجد ، ص ٨٨، نمبر ٣٢) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے مسجد میں بیع و شراء نہیں کرنا چاہیئے ۔ اس لئے سامان تجارت کو لا نا بھی مکروہ ہے۔
Chapter of I'tikaf (1139) And it is disapproved to bring the sold commodity into it, and it is disapproved to make a contract for what was for trade. Explanation: For the mu'takif, bringing trade goods into the mosque is makruh, because it creates an atmosphere of trade instead of i'tikaf. And if there is no need, speaking about buying and selling is also makruh. Evidence: (1) In a hadith: from Wathila ibn al-Asqa' that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Keep your mosques free from your children, your madmen, your evil ones, your buying and selling, your disputes, raising voices, executing punishments, drawing swords; and place at their doors places for purification, and perfume them on Fridays.' (Ibn Majah, Bab ma yukrah fi al-masajid, p. 107 no. 750) This hadith indicates to keep mosques free from buying and selling. (2) Another hadith: from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited buying and selling in the mosque. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-takhalluq yawm al-jumu'ah, p. 163 no. 079; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi karahiyat al-bay' wa al-shira', p. 88 no. 32) This hadith also indicates that buying and selling should not be done in the mosque, so bringing trade goods is also makruh.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This is a ruling with proofs from the Sunnah. The author (Thamaratun Najah) states that for a person in i'tikaf (seclusion in the mosque for worship), it is makruh (disapproved) to bring goods for sale into the mosque and to conduct any trade transaction. The reason is that such activities change the atmosphere from worship to commerce. Even speaking about buying and selling without necessity is makruh. Two hadith are cited: one explicitly commands to keep mosques free from buying and selling, and the other narrates a specific prohibition. Based on these, the Hanafi ruling is that such actions are makruh, and they should be avoided to preserve the sanctity of i'tikaf.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): A legal category meaning 'disliked' or 'disapproved'; here it is makruh tanzih, which is not sinful but better avoided.
اعتكاف (i'tikaf): Seclusion in the mosque for worship, usually for a specified period, with intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Wajib (obligatory) if one needs to sell

Key Takeaway
Trade in the mosque during i'tikaf is makruh tanzih, based on explicit hadith commands to keep mosques free from commerce.

Nadhr for Days of I'tikaf: Nights Binding Automatically
Ruling on a vow for day i'tikaf including its nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a vow for days of i'tikaf includes nights, explain the proofs (idiomatic usage, continuous nature of i'tikaf, and the effect of 'Ata'), and apply the exception for explicit exclusion.

Core Idea
A vow for days of i'tikaf automatically binds the nights because i'tikaf is continuous.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah: when someone vows i'tikaf for a number of days, the intervening nights are also obligatory unless explicitly excluded. The text provides three proofs: linguistic usage, the continuous nature of i'tikaf (tasalsul) compared to fasting, and the practice of the Salaf. Understanding this ruling clarifies the scope of nadhr in Hanafi fiqh and the principle of continuity in acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is vowing (nadhr) to perform i'tikaf for a specified number of days. The ruling is that the nights between those days become wajib automatically, unless the vower explicitly excludes them.
The hukm level is wajib (binding) – not fard, but obligatory due to the vow.
2
Examine the first proof – idiomatic usage
The text argues that in common Arabic usage, the word 'days' (ayam) can include nights. Therefore, when someone vows 'days of i'tikaf', the nights are included by default unless specified otherwise.
This is a linguistic proof (dalil lugawi).
3
Examine the second proof – nature of i'tikaf vs. fasting
The text contrasts i'tikaf with fasting. Fasting is only during the day and is intermittent (a gap at night), while i'tikaf involves both day and night and is continuous (tasalsul). Because i'tikaf is inherently continuous, a vow for days necessarily includes nights.
This is a talil (reasoning by virtue of the act's nature).
4
Examine the third proof – practice of the Salaf (Ata')
The text cites a report from 'Ata' that a mu'takif may stipulate i'tikaf only during the day and come to his family at night. This implies that without such a stipulation, the default is that nights are included.
This is an athar (precedent) supporting the default inclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٤٣) ولزمته الليالى ايضا بنذر اعتکاف ایام تشریح : کسی نے دن کے اعتکاف کی نذر مانی تو اس کی رات میں بھی اعتکاف کرنا ہو گا۔ مثلا چھ دنوں کا اعتکاف اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تو ان کی چھ راتوں کا اعتکاف بھی لازم ہوگا ، ہاں نذر مانتے وقت رات کا با ضابطہ انکار کیا تو اب رات کا اعتکاف لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه (۱) محاورے میں دن بولتا ہے تو اس میں رات بھی شامل ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے نیت کرنے والوں نے دن بولا تو اس کی رات بھی شامل ہوگی۔ اس لئے جتنے دنوں کی نیت ہے اس کی راتوں کا اعتکاف بھی لازم ہو گا (۲) روزہ متفرق طور پر ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ روزہ صرف دن میں ہوتا ہے اس کے بعد رات آتی ہے جس میں روزہ نہیں ہے اور دونوں کے درمیان فاصل ہے ۔ اس لئے روزہ متفرق طور پر ہوگا۔ لیکن اعتکاف رات اور دن دونوں میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ مسلسل ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اعتکاف میں تسلسل ہے تسلسل کی نیت نہ کی ہو (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عطاء فى المعتكف يشترط ان يعتكف بالنهار ويأتى اهله ہے۔ چاہیے
(1143) And the nights are also binding upon a vow of i'tikaf for days. Explanation: If someone vows i'tikaf for days, then he must also observe i'tikaf during the nights. For example, if he obligated himself to i'tikaf for six days, then the six nights become binding as well. However, if at the time of vowing he explicitly excludes the nights, then the nights are not required. Evidence: (1) Idiomatically, when one says 'days', nights are included. So if he intended days, the nights are also included. (2) Fasting is separate from night because fasting is only during the day, then night comes without fasting, so fasting is intermittent. But i'tikaf includes both day and night, so it is continuous. Thus, continuity is required in i'tikaf even if not explicitly intended. (3) According to 'Ata', regarding a mu'takif who stipulates that he will do i'tikaf in the day and come to his family (at night)...
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This ruling deals with the case where a person makes a nadhr (vow) to perform i'tikaf for a certain number of days. In Hanafi fiqh, such a vow automatically requires i'tikaf for the nights that intervene between those days, because i'tikaf is a continuous act. The commentary explains that in common usage, 'days' may include nights, and more importantly, the nature of i'tikaf is different from fasting: fasting is only during the day, so a vow of fasting does not include nights, but i'tikaf encompasses both day and night, so it must be continuous. However, if the person explicitly excludes the nights in his vow, then they are not necessary. The proof is from the practice of Salaf (Ata') who considered it valid to stipulate only days, implying that without stipulation, nights are included. The Hanafi school thus holds that a general vow for days of i'tikaf includes its nights.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship that is not obligatory in itself.
تسلسل (tasalsul): Continuity; i'tikaf must be continuous without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The nights are not binding because the vow was only for days
B) The nights are binding as part of the vow because i'tikaf is continuous
C) The nights are optional; one may choose to include them
D) The vow is invalid if nights are not specified

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a vow for days of i'tikaf automatically obligates the nights, because i'tikaf is a continuous act; only explicit exclusion removes the nights.

Nullification of I'tikaf by Intercourse and its Preludes
Ruling on what nullifies i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two actions that nullify i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from Quran and Companion saying.

Core Idea
Intercourse and ejaculation from its preludes nullify i'tikaf — both require starting anew.

This lesson addresses a critical aspect of i'tikaf: what actions break it. While many know that intercourse invalidates i'tikaf, the Hanafi school extends the ruling to include ejaculation caused by direct physical contact with desire. We will examine the Quranic prohibition and the Companion's explanation to understand the full scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage states that i'tikaf is nullified (batil) by two things: actual intercourse (wata') and ejaculation (inzal) resulting from its preludes (dawa'i al-wata'), such as kissing with desire.
Note that the ruling is that the i'tikaf becomes completely invalid, not merely sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The first evidence is the Quranic verse (2:187) prohibiting sexual contact during i'tikaf. The second is the saying of Ibn Abbas (radiallahu 'anhu) that if a mu'takif has intercourse, his i'tikaf is invalidated and he must start anew.
Both proofs are cited in order of strength: Quran (qat'i al-thubut) then Companion's opinion.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's imperative 'لا تباشروهن' is a prohibition; in Hanafi usul, a prohibition concerning an inherent part of worship indicates nullification. The Companion's saying clarifies that the nullification applies to intercourse and, by analogy, to any deliberate act leading to ejaculation.
The key linguistic point: 'mubashara' (direct contact) is understood broadly to include preludes when they result in ejaculation.
4
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
The passage indicates that the nullification by intercourse is agreed upon (muttafaq 'alayh) among schools. The Hanafi addition of preludes leading to ejaculation is a distinctive position, but other schools may limit nullification to actual intercourse only.
This difference does not affect the core ruling but shows the Hanafi reliance on maqasid and qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٤٢) وبطل بوطئه وبالانزال بدواعيه تشریح : ولی کر لے تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا، یا دواعی ولی سے انزال ہو جائے تب بھی اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا، مثلا بوسہ لیا جس سے انزال ہوا تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ ولا تباشروهن وانتم عاكفون في المساجد . ( آیت ١٨٧ سورۃ البقرۃ ٢) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعتکاف کی حالت میں مباشرت کرنے سے اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ (۲) قول صحابی میں ہے۔عن ابن عباس قال اذا جامع المعتكف ابطل اعتكافه واستأنف. (مصنف ابن ابی هیة ۹۲ ما قالوا فی المختلف بیجا مع ما علیه فی ذلک ج ثانی ص ١٣٣٨، نمبر ۹۶۸۰) معتکف جماع کرے تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا اب پھر سے اعتکاف کرے۔(۳) عن ابن عباس قال اذا وقع المعتكف على امرأته استأنف اعتكافه (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب وقوعه علی امرانته، ج رابع ، ص ٢٧٩، نمبر ٨١١١ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۹ ما قالوافی المختلف مجامع ما علیه فی ذلک ج ثانی ص ١٣٣٨ نمبر ۹۶۸۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بیوی سے جماع کیا تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا اور دوبارہ اعتکاف شروع کرے۔
(1142) And it is nullified by intercourse and by ejaculation due to its causes. Explanation: If one engages in intercourse, i'tikaf is invalidated. Or if ejaculation occurs due to its causes (like kissing), then also i'tikaf is invalidated. For example, kissing that leads to ejaculation nullifies i'tikaf. Evidence: (1) In the verse: 'And do not have sexual relations with them while you are secluded in the mosques' (Quran 2:187). This verse indicates that intercourse during i'tikaf nullifies it. (2) Saying of a Companion: Ibn Abbas said: 'If the mu'takif has intercourse, his i'tikaf is invalidated and he must start anew.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 92, no. 9680) (3) Also from Ibn Abbas: 'When the mu'takif has intercourse with his wife, he must start his i'tikaf anew.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 8111; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 9680) This shows that intercourse invalidates i'tikaf and requires a fresh start.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This is a ruling on the nullification of i'tikaf. The mu'takif's i'tikaf becomes invalid (batil) in two cases: (1) actual intercourse (wata'), and (2) ejaculation (inzal) occurring due to preludes such as kissing or touching with desire. The evidence includes the Quranic verse that explicitly prohibits sexual contact during i'tikaf, implying that any such act nullifies the state. Additionally, the saying of Ibn Abbas (a Companion) confirms that intercourse requires starting the i'tikaf anew. The Hanafi school holds that even minor contact leading to ejaculation nullifies i'tikaf, as it falls under the prohibition of 'mubashara' (direct contact).

Key Terms
وطء (wata'): Sexual intercourse; the act that invalidates i'tikaf.
دواعي الوطء (dawa'i al-wata'): Preludes to intercourse, such as kissing, touching, etc., that lead to ejaculation.
مباشرة (mubashara): Direct contact; the term used in the Quranic prohibition, understood broadly by Hanafis to include any intimate contact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Speaking to one's spouse without desire

Key Takeaway
Intercourse and ejaculation from its deliberate preludes nullify i'tikaf completely, requiring a fresh start.

Nullification of I'tikaf by Intercourse and Ejaculation
Ruling on nullification of i'tikaf with Quranic and Companion evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two actions that nullify i'tikaf and explain the Quranic and Companion evidence for each.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is nullified by intercourse and by ejaculation from foreplay, based on the Quran and sayings of Ibn Abbas.

Maintaining the validity of i'tikaf requires avoiding all forms of sexual activity, even those that do not culminate in intercourse. This lesson clarifies the precise acts that break i'tikaf, grounding the ruling in divine command and Companion practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The author states that i'tikaf is nullified by intercourse and by ejaculation resulting from foreplay (dawa'i). Determine the legal consequence: i'tikaf becomes batil (invalid).
2
Locate the primary evidence (Quran)
The verse 'Wa la tubaashiruuhunna wa antum 'aakifoona fil masaajid' (2:187) prohibits direct contact. Note that the word 'tubaashir' encompasses all forms of physical intimacy.
This verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah in its application to all foreplay.
3
Analyze the Companion sayings
Two athar from Ibn Abbas state that if a mu'takif has intercourse, he must renew his i'tikaf. These serve as secondary evidence (qawl sahabi) reinforcing the ruling.
Companion sayings are a source in Hanafi usul when not contradicted by stronger evidence.
4
Derive the ruling for ejaculation from foreplay
The text extends the ruling to ejaculation resulting from incitements like kissing, even without full intercourse. This is based on the principle that any act contradicting the spirit of seclusion invalidates i'tikaf.
Hanafis consider the cause (sabab) to be the deliberate pursuit of sexual pleasure that culminates in emission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۴۲) وبطل بوطئه وبالانزال بدواعيه (۱۱۴۲) اور اعتکاف باطل ہو جائے گا، وہی سے اور دوائی ولی سے انزال ہو جانے سے۔ تشریح : ولی کر لے تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا، یا دواعی ولی سے انزال ہو جائے تب بھی اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا، مثلا بوسہ لیا جس سے انزال ہوا تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ ولا تباشروهن وانتم عاكفون في المساجد . ( آیت ۱۸۷ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعتکاف کی حالت میں مباشرت کرنے سے اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ (۲) قول صحابی میں ہے۔عن ابن عباس قال اذا جامع المعتكف ابطل اعتكافه واستأنف. (مصنف ابن ابی هیة ۹۲ ما قالوا فی المختلف بیجا مع ما علیه فی ذلک ج ثانی ص ۱۳۳۸، نمبر ۹۶۸۰) معتکف جماع کرے تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا اب پھر سے اعتکاف کرے۔(۳) عن ابن عباس قال اذا وقع المعتكف على امرأته استأنف اعتكافه (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب وقوعه علی امرانته، ج رابع ، ص ۲۷۹، نمبر ۸۱۱۱ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۹ ما قالوافی المختلف مجامع ما علیه فی ذلک ج ثانی ص ۱۳۳۸ نمبر ۹۶۸۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بیوی سے جماع کیا تو اعتکاف ٹوٹ جائے گا اور دوبارہ اعتکاف شروع کرے۔
And it is invalidated by his intercourse and by ejaculation due to its incitements. (1142) And i'tikaf will become invalid by intercourse and by ejaculation from foreplay. Explanation: If he has intercourse, i'tikaf will break; or if ejaculation occurs from foreplay, then also i'tikaf will break, for example, if he kissed which led to ejaculation, then i'tikaf will break. Evidence: (1) In the verse: 'And do not have relations with them while you are i'tikaf in the mosques.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187) From this verse it is understood that during i'tikaf, touching/intercourse breaks i'tikaf. (2) In the saying of a Companion: From Ibn Abbas: 'If the mu'takif has intercourse, he invalidates his i'tikaf and starts anew.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...). (3) From Ibn Abbas: 'If the mu'takif has intercourse with his wife, he renews his i'tikaf.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq...) In this athar, it is mentioned that if he had intercourse with his wife, i'tikaf breaks and he should start i'tikaf again.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The author states that i'tikaf is nullified by intercourse (wat') and by ejaculation (inzal) resulting from foreplay (dawa'ihi). The Urdu explanation clarifies that either actual intercourse or ejaculation from actions like kissing breaks i'tikaf. The evidence first cites Quran 2:187, where 'tubaashir' (to have relations) implicitly includes any direct contact leading to sexual gratification. Then two athar from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) are quoted, stating explicitly that if a mu'takif has intercourse, his i'tikaf is invalidated and he must start anew. This establishes the ruling firmly in the Hanafi school. Note that the term 'dawa'ihi' refers to incitements or actions that lead to ejaculation, such as hugging or kissing with desire.

Key Terms
بوطئه (biwat'ihi): His sexual intercourse; the act of copulation.
انزال (inzāl): Ejaculation of semen.
دواعیه (dawā'īhi): Its incitements; actions that lead to sexual desire and possible ejaculation, such as kissing, hugging, etc.

I'tikaf is nullified by both intercourse and deliberate ejaculation from foreplay, based on Quran and Companion sayings.

Vowing Days of I'tikaf Includes Nights
Ruling that vowing days of i'tikaf includes the intervening nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that vowing i'tikaf for days obligates the nights, and explain the proofs based on 'urf and qiyas.

Core Idea
Vowing days of i'tikaf automatically includes nights due to customary usage and the continuous nature of i'tikaf

When someone vows to perform i'tikaf for a number of days, a natural question arises: are the nights of those days also required? The Hanafi school answers with a clear 'yes' – based on how people commonly speak and the unique character of i'tikaf as an act that spans both day and night. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its proofs, and the one exception: explicit exclusion of the nights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is vowing i'tikaf for a specified number of days. The ruling is that the nights of those days become wajib as part of the same vow.
2
Locate the Proofs
Three proofs are cited: (1) common usage ('urf) where 'day' often includes night, (2) analogy (qiyas) with i'tikaf's continuous nature compared to fasting, and (3) an athar from 'Ata about stipulating day-only i'tikaf.
The athar is cut off but supports the idea that if one stipulates only days, nights can be excluded.
3
Understand the Exception
If the vower explicitly excludes the nights at the time of vowing (e.g., 'I vow i'tikaf for days only'), then the nights are not obligatory.
This exception shows that the default inclusion is based on linguistic custom and the nature of i'tikaf, not an absolute rule.
4
Apply the Ruling
Take an example: a person vows six days of i'tikaf. He must perform i'tikaf for six days and the six nights in between. If he completes only six days, his vow is not fulfilled until he makes up the nights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۱۴۳) دنوں کے (اعتکاف کی ) منت سے راتوں کا ( اعتکاف بھی لازم ہو جائے گا۔ تشريح کسی نے دن کے اعتکاف کی نذر مانی تو اس کی رات میں بھی اعتکاف کرنا ہو گا۔ مثلا چھ دنوں کا اعتکاف اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تو ان کی چھ راتوں کا اعتکاف بھی لازم ہوگا ، ہاں نذر مانتے وقت رات کا با ضابطہ انکار کیا تو اب رات کا اعتکاف لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه (۱) محاورے میں دن بولتا ہے تو اس میں رات بھی شامل ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے نیت کرنے والوں نے دن بولا تو اس کی رات بھی شامل ہوگی۔ اس لئے جتنے دنوں کی نیت کی ہے اس کی راتوں کا اعتکاف بھی لازم ہو گا (۲) روزہ متفرق طور پر ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ روزہ صرف دن میں ہوتا ہے اس کے بعد رات آتی ہے جس میں روزہ نہیں ہے اور دونوں کے درمیان فاصل ہے ۔ اس لئے روزہ متفرق طور پر ہوگا۔ لیکن اعتکاف رات اور دن دونوں میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ مسلسل ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اعتکاف میں تسلسل ہے تسلسل کی نیت نہ کی ہو (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عطاء فى المعتكف يشترط ان يعتكف بالنهار ويأتى اهله ہے۔ چاہیے
Translation: (1143) By vowing i'tikaf of days, the nights also become obligatory. Explanation: If someone vows i'tikaf of days, then he must also perform i'tikaf during the nights. For example, if he obligated upon himself i'tikaf of six days, then i'tikaf of those six nights is also obligatory. Yes, if at the time of vowing he explicitly excludes the nights, then i'tikaf of the nights is not obligatory. Evidence: (1) In common usage, when 'day' is said, night is included in it. Therefore, when the one vowing said 'day', its night is included. Thus, for however many days he intended, i'tikaf of those nights is also obligatory. (2) Fasting occurs separately because fasting is only during the day, then night comes in which there is no fast, and there is a gap between them. Therefore, fasting occurs as separate units. But i'tikaf occurs in both night and day, so it is continuous. Therefore, i'tikaf requires continuity, even if he did not intend continuity. (3) There is an athar: From 'Ata, regarding the mu'takif who stipulates that he will perform i'tikaf by day and visit his family...
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage addresses a nuanced issue: if someone vows i'tikaf for a specified number of days, do the nights of those days automatically become part of the obligation? The answer is yes, based on customary usage ('urf) where 'day' often encompasses the following night. The author gives an example of six days obligating six nights. However, an exception is made if the vower explicitly excludes the nights at the time of vowing. The proof includes reasoning by comparison with fasting: fasting is only during the day, so it can be discontinuous, but i'tikaf is performed in the mosque continuously, so it requires inclusion of the night. An athar from 'Ata is cited to support this, though its text is cut off.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow; making a specific act of worship obligatory upon oneself by a pledge.
تسلسل (tasalsul): Continuity; the state of being consecutive without break.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The nights are not obligatory
B) The nights are obligatory and must be included
C) It depends on the intention at the time of vowing
D) The vow is invalid

Key Takeaway
Vowing days of i'tikaf automatically obligates the intervening nights unless explicitly excluded, based on customary usage and the continuous nature of i'tikaf.

Quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr
Ruling with proof on quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from hadith that establishes this ruling.

Core Idea
Half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of other grains: the Hanafi measure for Sadaqat al-Fitr is fixed.

Sadaqat al-Fitr is a wajib charity at the end of Ramadan. The Hanafi school specifies precise quantities based on prophetic hadith and the practice of the Companions. This lesson examines the required amounts—half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or sawiq) and one sa' of dates, raisins, or barley—and the evidence that supports them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
The passage states that Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib. Note the specific quantities: half a sa' of wheat (and its flour or sawiq) or one sa' of dates, raisins, or barley.
Wheat derivatives count as wheat; other grains require a full sa'.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (Bukhari and Muslim) which originally mentioned a sa' of each type. Then note the hadith of Abu Saghir (Abu Dawood) specifying half a sa' of wheat per person.
3
Understand the reason for the distinction
The commentary explains that wheat was scarce and expensive, so half a sa' was fixed; dates and barley were abundant, so a full sa' was prescribed.
The rationale is based on the economic conditions of the time.
4
Analyze the additional proofs
Consider the athar from Ibn 'Umar and 'Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz regarding the mukatib, which establish that Sadaqat al-Fitr is linked to maintenance and that the mukatib is not liable.
These show the principle of obligation based on maintenance.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki) require one sa' of wheat as well. The Hanafi school relies on the specific hadith of Abu Saghir and the later consensus on half a sa'.
This difference arises from prioritizing different hadith and their interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صدقة الفطر الكبير وزوجته وقنّ مشترک و آبق الا بعد عوده وكذا المغصوب والماسور (۱۲۱۳) وهى نصف صاع من بر ودقيقه او سويقه او صاع تمر او زبيب او شعير وجه: (1) اثر میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر انه كان يودى زکوۃ الفطر عن كل مملوک له فی ارضه و غير ارضه وعن كل انسان يعوله من صغيرا وكبير وعن رقيق امرأته وكان له مكاتب بالمدينة فكان لا يودى عنه - سن البیهقی ، باب من قال لا يودي عن مکاتب ج رابع ص ۲۷۲، نمبر ۷۶۸۶ رمصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ہ۷۳ ما قالوا فی المکاتب یعطی عنہ یودی تتبرج قالوافی سیده ام لاج ثانی ص ۴۰۰ نمبر ۱۰۳۸۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر مکاتب کا صدقہ الفطر خود ادا نہیں کرتے تھے ۔ کیونکہ وہ ان کی مونت میں نہیں تھا۔ (۲) ان عمر بن عبد العزيز قال : ليس فى مال المكاتب زكوة . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲ ۵ في المكاتب من قال : ليس عليه زکوۃ ج ثانی ص ۱۳۸۷ نمبر ۱۰۲۲۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مکاتب کے مال میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے اور صدقۃ الفطر بھی زکوۃ کا ایک حصہ ہے اس لئے صدقۃ الفطر بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ صدقۃ الفطر کی مقدار کے ترجمه :(۱۲۱۳) صدقہ فطر کی مقدار آدھا صاع گیہوں یا گیہوں کا آنا، یاستو ہے۔ یا ایک صاع کھجور یاکشمش ، یا کو ہے۔ تشریح : آدھا صاع گیہوں ہو یا اس کا آٹا ہو یا اس کا ستو ہو تو چونکہ وہ گیہوں کی جنس سے ہے اس لئے آدھا صاع ہی کافی ہے، البتہ کھجور اور جو ایک صاع ہونا چاہئے ، اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عرب میں کھجور اور جو پیدا ہوتا تھا اس لئے یہ چیزیں ستی تھیں، اس لئے ایک صاع قرار دیا، اور گیہوں کی پیداوار کم تھی اس لئے یہ مہنگا تھا اس لئے آدھا صاع مقر فر مایا۔ اس وقت گیہوں اگر چہ کھجور کے مقابلے پرستا ہے لیکن چونکہ حدیث میں وہ معیار مقرر کر دیا ہے اس لئے وہی معیار رہے گا۔ اور کشمش کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے جو آگے آرہا ہے۔ وجه: (ا) عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال كنا نعطيها في زمان النبي الله صاعا من طعام أو صاعا من تمر أو صاعا من شعير أو صاعا من زبيب فلما جاء معاوية و جائت السمراء قال أرى مدا من هذا يعدل مدين ( بخاری شریف ، باب صاعا من زبیب ص ۲۴۵ نمبر ۱۵۰۸ مسلم شریف ، باب زكاة الفطر على المسلمين من النمر والشعير ص ۳۹۶ نمبر ۲۲۸۳/۹۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک صاع گیہوں اور ایک صاع کھجور اور ایک صاع کشمش فطرہ میں دیتے تھے بعد میں ایک صاع گیہوں دو آدمیوں کے لئے کر دیا ، یعنی آدھا صاع ایک آدمی کے لئے اور اس پر اجماع بھی ہو گیا۔ (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی صغیر قال قال رسول الله صاع من بر او قمح علی کل اثنین صغیر او كبير. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من روی نصف صاع من تتح ص ۳۳۵ نمبر ۱۶۱۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ خود حضور نے آدھا صاع گیہوں فطرہ کے لئے متعین فرمایا۔ (۳) اور آٹے کا تذکرہ اس اثر میں ہے۔ سألت عبد الله بن شداد عن صدقة الفطر فقال : نصف صاع من حنطة أو دقيق - ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی صدقۃ الفطر من قال : نصف صاع بر ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۳۹۷، نمبر ۱۰۳۴۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گیہوں یا آٹا آدھا صاع ہے، اس لئے گیہوں کا آنا ہی مراد ہے۔ لغت :بر: گیہوں۔ دقیق: آٹا۔ سویق : ستو۔ زبیب کشمش، یہ انگور کوسکھا کر بناتے ہیں ۔شعیر: جو۔
Chapter of Sadaqat al-Fitr. The adult, his wife, a jointly owned slave, and an absconding slave (except after his return) and similarly a usurped slave and a captive slave. (1213) And it is half a sa' of wheat and its flour or its sawiq, or a sa' of dates or raisins or barley. Evidence: (1) There is a report: from Ibn 'Umar that he used to pay Zakat al-Fitr for every slave he owned in his land and outside his land, and for every person he supported, young and old, and for the slaves of his wife, and he had a mukatib in Medina and he would not pay for him. [Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: He who said do not pay for a mukatib, vol. 4, p. 272, no. 7686; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, hadith 73, what they said about the mukatib: is zakat paid for him? They said: his master pays, vol. 2, p. 400, no. 10386] From this report it is understood that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar did not pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his mukatib himself, because he was not under his maintenance. (2) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz said: There is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatib. [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 2:5 on the mukatib: He who said there is no zakat upon him, vol. 2, p. 1387, no. 10229] In this report it is stated that there is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatib, and Sadaqat al-Fitr is also a part of zakat, therefore there will be no Sadaqat al-Fitr either. Regarding the quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr: Translation of (1213): The quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr is half a sa' of wheat or its flour, or sawiq, or one sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. Explanation: Half a sa' of wheat, or its flour, or its sawiq, since it is of the genus of wheat, half a sa' is sufficient. However, dates and barley should be one sa'. The reason is that in Arabia, dates and barley were produced, so these things were abundant, therefore one sa' was prescribed. Wheat production was less, so it was expensive, therefore half a sa' was fixed. At this time, even if wheat is cheaper than dates, since the standard was set in the hadith, that standard will remain. There is a difference of opinion regarding raisins which will come later. Evidence: (a) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: We used to give it in the time of the Prophet (PBUH) a sa' of food, or a sa' of dates, or a sa' of barley, or a sa' of raisins. When Mu'awiya came and the Syrian wheat came, he said: I consider one mudd of this equal to two mudds. [Bukhari, chapter: a sa' of raisins, p. 245, no. 1508; Muslim, chapter: Zakat al-Fitr on Muslims from dates and barley, p. 396, no. 2283/985] In this hadith it is stated that they used to give one sa' of wheat, one sa' of dates, and one sa' of raisins for Fitra. Later, one sa' of wheat was made for two people, i.e., half a sa' for one person, and there was consensus on this. (2) Another hadith: From Abu Saghir, the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: A sa' of wheat or barley for every two people, young or old. [Abu Dawood, chapter: Whoever narrated half a sa' of wheat, p. 335, no. 1619] In this hadith, the Prophet himself fixed half a sa' of wheat for Fitra. (3) The mention of flour is in this report: I asked 'Abdullah ibn Shaddad about Sadaqat al-Fitr, and he said: Half a sa' of wheat or flour. [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on Sadaqat al-Fitr: He who said half a sa' of wheat, vol. 2, p. 1397, no. 10349] In this report, half a sa' is for wheat or flour, so flour is also meant. Vocabulary: بر: wheat. دقیق: flour. سویق: sawiq. زبیب: raisins, made by drying grapes. شعیر: barley.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr with proofs from hadith and athar. The matn states that the obligatory amount is half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or sawiq) or one sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. The author then provides evidence: (1) The practice of Ibn 'Umar not paying for his mukatib, indicating that Sadaqat al-Fitr is tied to maintenance; (2) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz's statement that a mukatib's wealth has no zakat, establishing that Sadaqat al-Fitr follows the same ruling. The explanation clarifies that the half sa' for wheat is based on scarcity and higher value, while the full sa' for dates and barley reflects their abundance. The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri shows the original practice of one sa' each, later modified by Mu'awiya to half a sa' of wheat, and consensus was reached on that. The hadith of Abu Saghir explicitly fixes half a sa' of wheat per person. The report of 'Abdullah ibn Shaddad confirms that flour is included as wheat. The passage concludes with vocabulary definitions.

Key Terms
صدقۃ الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): A wajib charity given at the end of Ramadan by every eligible Muslim on behalf of himself and his dependents.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; in the Hanafi school, one sa' equals four mudds, equivalent to eight Iraqi ratls (approximately 3.2 liters or 2.6 kg for wheat).
مکاتب (mukatib): A slave who has entered a contract of manumission (kitaba) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in installments for his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the required amount of Sadaqat al-Fitr for wheat?
A) One sa'
B) Half a sa'
C) Two mudds
D) One mudd

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's quantity for Sadaqat al-Fitr is half a sa' of wheat (or its equivalents) and one sa' of other grains, based on prophetic hadith and early practice.

The Measure of the Sa' in Sadaqat al-Fitr: The Eight-Ratl vs. Five-and-One-Third Ratl Dispute
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute over the weight of the sa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sa' weight, identify the proofs cited by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school adopts the eight-ratl sa' for Sadaqat al-Fitr, but Abu Yusuf differed, making the exact measure a matter of ijtihad within the school.

In this passage, we explore a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the weight of the sa' used for Sadaqat al-Fitr. While all scholars agree a sa' is four mudds, the weight in ratls is contested: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say eight ratls, while Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i say five and one-third. The proofs involve explicit hadith and estimates, and the difference affects the actual amount of food given.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed-upon definition
Identify that all schools agree a sa' is four mudds, but disagree on the weight. This is the foundation of the dispute.
2
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school
Name the positions: eight ratls (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) vs. five and one-third ratls (Abu Yusuf).
Abu Yusuf's position aligns with the Shafi'i school.
3
Examine the proofs for the eight-ratl view
Analyze the hadith of Anas (wudu with two ratls, ghusl with a sa' of eight ratls) and the report of 'Umar's sa' being eight ratls. Understand why these are considered strong evidence.
The hadith of Anas is explicit numerical evidence.
4
Examine the proofs for the five-and-one-third ratl view
Analyze the hadith of Abu Hurayra (the Medinan sa' is the smallest) and Malik's estimation of the Prophet's sa' at five and one-third ratls. Understand the counterarguments.
Malik's estimation is a personal ijtihad, not an explicit text.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: the amount of Sadaqat al-Fitr (e.g., wheat) is larger with eight ratls. The Hanafi school officially follows the eight-ratl view as mufta bihi.

Translation of (1214): And it is eight ratls by the Iraqi (standard). From whoever narrated half a sa' of wheat, p. 335, no. 1619) In this hadith it is stated that the Prophet himself fixed half a sa' of wheat for Fitra. (3) The mention of flour is in this report: I asked 'Abdullah ibn Shaddad about Sadaqat al-Fitr, and he said: Half a sa' of wheat or flour. [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on Sadaqat al-Fitr: He who said half a sa' of wheat, vol. 2, p. 1397, no. 10349] In this report, half a sa' is for wheat or flour, so flour is also meant. According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf, one sa' is five and one-third ratls. Evidence: (1) From Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet (PBUH) used to perform wudu with two ratls and ghusl with a sa' of eight ratls. [Darqutni, book of Zakat al-Fitr, vol. 2, p. 134, no. 2120/2119; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what indicates that the Prophet's sa' was five and one-third ratls, vol. 4, p. 287, no. 7724] From this hadith it is understood that the sa' should be eight ratls. (2) The report of 'Umar which the author of al-Hidayah presented: I heard Hanash saying: The sa' of 'Umar is eight ratls, and Sharik said: More than seven ratls and less than eight. [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter 115 on what is the sa', vol. 2, p. 422, no. 10643] In this report, the sa' is eight ratls. The evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf: (1) From Ibn Hibban, in Nasb al-Rayah, this hadith: from Abu Hurayra that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) was asked: O Messenger of Allah, our sa' is the smallest of sa's and our mudd is the largest of mudds, so he said: O Allah, bless us in our sa' and bless us in our little and much, and give us with blessing two blessings. [Ibn Hibban in his Sahih, in the 29th type of the fourth section, Nasb al-Rayah, chapter of Sadaqat al-Fitr, vol. 2, p. 446] In this hadith it is stated that our sa' is a small sa'. (2) This hadith is also evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf: My father narrated from his mother that she presented this sa' to the Messenger of Allah. Malik said: I estimated it and found it five and one-third ratls. [Darqutni, book of Zakat al-Fitr, p. 132, no. 2105; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what indicates that the Prophet's sa' was five and one-third ratls, p. 287, no. 772] From this hadith it is known that the Prophet's sa' was five and one-third ratls. The majority of imams act upon this. (3) Another evidence they have: He said: We came to Abu Yusuf from Hajj, and we came to him. He said: I want to open a chapter of knowledge for you. I investigated it and came to Medina and asked about the sa', and they said... [Text cuts off]
