Chapter on visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him). (1493) Then he stands at the head of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as before and says: O Allah, You said—and Your word is truth—'And if, when they wronged themselves, they had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah accepting repentance and merciful.' And we have come to You, hearing Your word, obedient to Your command, seeking intercession through Your Prophet to You. O Allah, our Lord, forgive us and our fathers and our mothers and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and place not in our hearts any rancor toward those who believe. Our Lord, You are kind and merciful. Our Lord, give us good in this world and good in the Hereafter, and protect us from the punishment of the Fire. Exalted is your Lord, the Lord of majesty, above what they describe. And peace be upon the messengers. And praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. (1494) And he may add whatever he wishes and supplicate with what is present, and he will be granted success by Allah's grace. Commentary: Then he comes near the head of the Prophet and supplicates as before. Evidence: (1) The above supplications are from these verses: 'And if, when they wronged themselves...' (Quran 4:64) (2) 'They say, Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith...' (Quran 59:10) (3) Some say, 'Our Lord, give us good in this world...' (Quran 2:201) (4) 'Exalted is your Lord...' (Quran 37:180-182). 'Ghil' means rancor. Translation: (1494) If he wishes, he may increase these supplications, and supplicate with what he remembers and is granted success by Allah.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage describes the sunnah of visiting the Prophet's grave. The visitor stands at the head of the Prophet (peace be upon him), facing him, and recites a composite du'a drawing from several Quranic verses. The first part invokes the verse about seeking forgiveness (4:64), indicating that coming to the Prophet and seeking forgiveness through him is a means of obtaining divine mercy. The supplication continues with verses asking for forgiveness for all believers (59:10), for good in both worlds (2:201), and ends with glorification (37:180-182). The commentary notes that the visitor may add any other supplications. This practice is rooted in the Quranic permission to seek intercession through the Prophet's person, as understood by the Hanafi school. The text also clarifies that the word 'ghil' means rancor or ill-feeling.

Key Terms
غِلا (ghila): Rancor, ill-feeling, or malice.
اسطوانة (ustuwānah): Pillar or column in the Prophet's mosque associated with a historical event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Makruh
D) Haram

Key Takeaway

Visiting the Pillar of Abu Lubabah
Ruling with proof for visiting a specific location in the mosque.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions at the Pillar of Abu Lubabah and cite the Quranic proof for its virtue.

Core Idea
Praying and repenting at the Pillar of Abu Lubabah is a recommended act linked to an accepted repentance.

This lesson focuses on a specific practice in the Prophet's Mosque: visiting the pillar known as Ustuwanat Abi Lubabah. It is a recommended act (mandub) to perform voluntary prayer, repent, and supplicate at this location, based on the historical event when the Companion Abu Lubabah tied himself there until his repentance was accepted. We will explore the ruling, its evidence from the Quran, and how to derive the recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended action
Read the passage carefully and list what the visitor is encouraged to do at the pillar. The text says: 'He prays as much nafl as he wishes, repents to Allah, and supplicates as he wishes.'
Focus on the verbs: يصلّي, يتوب, يدعو.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
The passage cites Quran 9:118, which mentions three Companions whose repentance was accepted. One of them is Abu Lubabah. Recognize that this verse forms the proof (dalil) for the significance of the location.
The verse is from Surah al-Tawbah, revealed regarding the acceptance of their repentance.
3
Connect the event to the ruling
Understand the link: Abu Lubabah tied himself to this pillar until his repentance was accepted (as per the historical account and the verse). Therefore, the place became associated with accepted repentance, making it recommended to perform acts of worship there.
The ruling is not based on explicit command but on the action of a Companion and the divine acceptance.
4
Note the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school considers this practice to be mandub (recommended), not obligatory. It is a sunnah derived from the actions of the Salaf, though some scholars view it as an innovation. The Hanafi stance is that it is permissible and meritorious.
The mufta bihi is 'recommended (mandub)'.

ترجمه : (1495) ثم يأتى اسطوانة ابى لبابة الّتي ربط بها نفسه حتى تاب سے معافی چاہتے اور رسول بھی ان کے لئے اللہ تعالی سے معافی چاہتے تو ضرور اللہ تعالی کو تو بہ قبول کرنے والا اور رحمت کرنے والا پاتے اے اللہ ہم آپ کے در پر آپ کے قول کو سن کر اطاعت کرتے ہوئے آئے ہیں ، آپ کے نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم سے آپ کی طرف شفاعت کی درخواست کرتے ہیں ،اے اللہ ہماری ، ہمارے باپوں کی ، ہماری ماؤں کی ، اور ہمارے ان بھائیوں کی جو ہم سے پہلے ایمان لا چکے ہیں اور ہمارے دلوں میں ایمان والوں کی طرف سے کینہ نہ ہونے دیجئے ، اے ہمارے رب آپ بڑے شفیق و رحیم ہیں۔ اے ہمارے پروردگار ہم کو دنیا میں بھی بہتری عنایت کیجئے اور آخرت میں بھی بہتری دیجئے اور ہم کو عذاب دوزخ سے بچائیے ، آپ کا رب جو بڑی عزت والا ہے ان باتوں سے پاک ہے جو یہ (کافر) بیان کرتے ہیں اور سلام ہو پیغمبروں پر اور تمامتر خوبیاں اللہ ہی کے لئے ہیں جو تمام عالم کا پروردگار ہے۔
ترجمه : (1495) ثم يأتى اسطوانة ابى لبابة الّتي ربط بها نفسه حتى تاب وهي بين القبر والمنبر ويصلّى ما شاء نفلا ويتوب الى الله ويدعو بما شاء.
تشریح : حضرت ابولبابہ نے اپنے تو بہ قبول ہونے تک اس ستون کے پاس باندھ رکھا تھا، اس لئے یہاں نفل پڑھے اور تو بہ کرے۔
وجه : حضرت ابولبابہ کے تو بہ قبول ہونے کے لئے یہ آیت نازل ہوئی تھی۔ و على الثلاثة الذين خلفوا حتى اذا ضاقت عليهم الارض بما رحبت و ضاقت عليهم انفسهم و ظنوا ان لا ملجاء من الله الا اليه ثم تاب عليهم ليتوبوا ان الله هو التواب الرحيم ۔ ( آیت ۱۱۸ ، سورۃ التوبۃ ۹)
Translation: (1495) Then he comes to the pillar of Abu Lubabah, to which he tied himself until he repented, and it is between the grave and the pulpit. He prays as much nafl as he wishes, repents to Allah, and supplicates as he wishes. Commentary: Hazrat Abu Lubabah tied himself to this pillar until his repentance was accepted; therefore, he prays nafl here and repents. Evidence: The following verse was revealed for the acceptance of Abu Lubabah's repentance: 'And upon the three who were left behind until the earth closed in on them with all its vastness and their souls were constricted, and they realized that there is no refuge from Allah except in Him. Then He turned to them so they might repent. Indeed, Allah is the Accepter of Repentance, the Merciful.' (Quran 9:118)
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage describes another recommended act: visiting the pillar known as 'Ustuwanat Abi Lubabah'. This pillar is located between the Prophet's grave and the minbar. It marks the spot where the Companion Abu Lubabah tied himself in remorse for a mistake until his repentance was accepted by Allah, as recorded in Quran 9:118. The visitor is encouraged to perform voluntary prayers (nafl), repent, and make supplication at this place. The commentary links this practice to the historical event and the verse, showing that this place carries spiritual significance as a site of accepted repentance. The text thus establishes the recommendation by connecting it to a specific divine acceptance.

Key Terms
اسطوانة أبي لبابة (ustuwānat abī lubābah): The pillar in the Prophet's mosque where Abu Lubabah tied himself until his repentance was accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the recommended actions at the Pillar of Abu Lubabah according to the passage?
A) Only recite Quran.
B) Perform nafl prayer, repent, and supplicate.
C) Make a vow.
D) Give charity.

Key Takeaway
The Pillar of Abu Lubabah is a site of accepted repentance, where it is recommended to pray nafl, repent, and make supplication.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Praying in the Rawdah (Garden of Paradise)
Describes the virtue and recommended acts in the Rawdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts in the Rawdah and identify the hadith evidence that establishes its virtue.

Core Idea
Pray and make dhikr in the Rawdah — it is a garden from Paradise by prophetic declaration.

This lesson focuses on the Rawdah, the blessed area in the Prophet's mosque. The Hanafi school recommends performing nafl prayers, supplications, and dhikr in this spot due to a sahih hadith. The source text presents the recommended acts and the prophetic evidence. By understanding this, you learn how a prophetic designation shapes recommended worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
The text instructs: come to the Rawdah, pray as much as you wish, supplicate, and increase in tasbih, tahlil, thana', and istighfar. These are the specific acts encouraged.
The acts are not limited; 'as much as you wish' indicates flexibility.
2
Cite the hadith evidence
The proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah in Sahih Muslim: 'What is between my house and my pulpit is a garden from the gardens of Paradise.' This establishes the Rawdah's unique virtue.
The hadith is authentic (sahih) and agreed upon by scholars.
3
Explain the evidence's implication
Because the Prophet designated this area a garden of Paradise, it is meritorious to perform worship there. The hadith does not command it, but strongly encourages it, hence the Hanafi ruling of sunnah muakkadah.
The virtue is attached to the location, not a specific act; any good deed is rewarded abundantly there.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (1496) ويأتي الروضة فيصلى ما شاء ويدعو بما احبّ ويُكثر من التسبيح والتهليل والثناء والاستغفار.
تشريح : ریاض الجنہ وہ جگہ ہے جس کے بارے میں حضور نے فرمایا کہ یہ جنت کا باغ ہے، اس جگہ آکر نماز پڑھے اور نبیح و تہلیل وغیرہ پڑھے۔
وجه : حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله الله قال ما بین بیتی و منبرى روضة من رياض الجنة و منبری علی حوضی ۔(مسلم شریف، باب فضل ما بین قبره و منبره وفضل موضع منبر ه ،ص۵۸۲، نمبر ۳۳۶۸/۱۳۹۰)
Translation: (1496) And he comes to the Rawdah, and prays as much as he wishes, and supplicates with what he loves, and increases in tasbih (glorification), tahlil (saying la ilaha illallah), thana' (praise), and istighfar (seeking forgiveness). Commentary: Rawdat al-Jannah is the place about which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'It is a garden from the gardens of Paradise.' He comes to this place, prays, and recites tasbih, tahlil, etc. Evidence: The hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'What is between my house and my pulpit is a garden from the gardens of Paradise, and my pulpit is upon my cistern.' (Sahih Muslim, 3368/1390)
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage covers the Rawdah, the area between the Prophet's house and his minbar, which is declared by a hadith to be a garden from Paradise. The visitor is encouraged to pray, supplicate, and engage in dhikr (tasbih, tahlil, thana', istighfar) abundantly. The proof is the authentic hadith in Sahih Muslim, which establishes the special virtue of this location. The Hanafi school considers it highly recommended to perform nafl prayers and dhikr here, following the general practice of the Salaf. The text emphasizes increasing worship in this blessed spot.

Key Terms
روضة (rawḍah): The area in the Prophet's mosque between his house and his pulpit, described as a garden of Paradise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended activity in the Rawdah according to the text?
A) Only pray fard salah.
B) Pray nafl, supplicate, and do dhikr abundantly.
C) Recite Quran loudly.
D) Give a sermon.

Key Takeaway
The Rawdah is a designated garden of Paradise; performing prayer and dhikr there is a sunnah muakkadah.
